root.App.Cache.genUrl = function (routeName, context) {
        var route = routeMap[routeName],
            path, keys, i, len, key, param, regex;

        if (!route) { return ''; }

        path = route.path;
        keys = route.keys;

        if (context &amp;&amp; (len = keys.length)) {
            for (i = 0; i &lt; len; i += 1) {
                key   = keys[i];
                param = key.name || key;
                regex = new RegExp('[:*]' + param + '\\b');
                path  = path.replace(regex, context[param]);
            }
        }

        // Replace missing params with empty strings.
        return path.replace(/([:*])([\w\-]+)?/g, '');
    };

He&#x2019;d come to present to my women&#x2019;s study group about being a cross-dresser. Among the four presenters was a postoperative transsexual, another cross-dressing man, and an androgynous individual, presenting partially as female, partially male.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EI found myself wildly attracted to the man in the purple dress. This was &#x201C;Deborah&quot;&#x2014;known to the rest of the world as &quot;David&quot;&#x2014;an orthopedic surgeon. Two years before, at 36, he&#x2019;d finally begun addressing the pain and self-loathing he felt from a profound inner conflict: For most of his life, he&#x2019;d wished he could be &quot;one of the girls.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIt was not Deborah&#x2019;s physical appearance to which I was drawn but the courage and honesty I witnessed that day. I was enrolled in personal-growth workshops and studying to become a psychotherapist, so yes, perhaps I was more open-minded than the average person. But more than that, I was attracted to someone finally being true to herself, sharing her deepest truth with a group of strangers. We parted with a hug, and I somehow knew we&#x2019;d meet again.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIt turned out that we had both signed up for an ongoing workshop called &#x201C;The Living Soul&#x201D; beginning the following month. I arrived and recognized David immediately, thinking how appealing he was as a man! During this intensive training workshop, David and I learned to know and understand ourselves more deeply, and we became closer through the process. The course encouraged digging within to acknowledge and appreciate our own inner workings, and our true natures were fully exposed to each other.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated:&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.glamour.com\u002Fsex-love-life\u002Fblogs\u002Fsmitten\u002F2015\u002F06\u002Fsigns-he-is-in-love-men-boyfriend?mbid=synd_yhealth\"\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003E25 Unmistakable Signs He&#x2019;s in Love With You\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EOutside of this situation, David was less open. At the time, he was married with four young children, and though this marriage wasn&#x2019;t working, he was not ready to end it. So we resisted acting on the smoldering physical attraction that developed between us. In 1988, realizing his marriage could not be saved, David ended it. We married in 1991, and we&#x2019;ve been together ever since.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBecause David&#x2019;s secret life had been revealed at our first meeting, it was no big deal seeing him in drag. We&#x2019;d go out with him dressed as Deborah for dinners with certain friends or an occasional weekend away. To me, my husband was &#x201C;just a cross-dresser.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBut, as with any relationship, it wasn&#x2019;t all easy. Our primary challenge (stepchildren and ex-spouses notwithstanding) was our sex life; specifically, the devastation David experienced whenever Deborah&#x2019;s time was over. I was delighted by the return of my man; his male persona was extremely masculine&#x2014;and I liked that. But sometimes I wanted something more traditional than a man in a nightgown coming to bed with me. I would ask if David could just be David once in a while. This created conflict and invariably sent him into a downward spiral. Usually, within days, David would find a way to come on to me and we&#x2019;d make love the way I wanted to. Then all would be well&#x2026;until the cycle repeated itself.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EPerhaps both of us were in denial about the magnitude of his need to be seen as a woman.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe breaking point came in fall 2009, when David was again considering a new therapist, a different antidepressant, some experimental method for accepting the grief of living a lie. As usual, he bemoaned this process, but something unusual happened; I shocked us both by saying, &#x201C;It&#x2019;s time to do something different.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated:&#xA0;\u003Cb\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.glamour.com\u002Fsex-love-life\u002F2008\u002F09\u002F10-things-hes-thinking-when-youre-naked?mbid=synd_yhealth\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003E10 Things He&#x2019;s Thinking When You&#x2019;re Naked\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EI suggested we talk to an endocrinologist. It was the first step toward resolving his now-60-year-long struggle and the beginning of a quest to honor the woman within. I&#x2019;d realized that my beloved would never be happy as a man, though I also knew that I could not commit to remaining in our marriage until I&#x2019;d experienced our new, changed life. I made this abundantly clear to him, not threatening or coercing but simply sharing it honestly, \u003Ci\u003Ebecause it was my truth.\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"405\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F38efe40b30a14b775747e6942c69dbf0a8c07ebb.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe next two years were a roller coaster ride for me. David told me many times, &#x201C;I&#x2019;ll stop this immediately if it means losing you.&#x201D; While I was touched by his willingness to forgo this dream, I knew that remaining married to an unhappy, inauthentic man was impossible. He had to move forward with his transition, but I still didn&#x2019;t know if I&#x2019;d be able to stay married to him once he did. We lived in this ambiguous state for more than two years until I realized that we belong together, regardless of anything.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EEver since Deborah formally came into the world in October 2011, she has been relentlessly happy. I&#x2019;ve accepted this new life of ours, even if it may not be my dream come true&#x2014;it&#x2019;s certainly hers. It&#x2019;s the life she thought would elude her forever, and I was able to support her as she made it a reality. For that reason, our marriage is one of my life&#x2019;s greatest achievements.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003ELeslie Hilburn Fabian is a clinical social worker and the author Choices\u003C\u002Fa\u003E)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ELegislation that would have allowed terminally ill patients to legally end their lives in California stalled Tuesday amid fierce opposition from religious groups.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe authors of the right-to-die bill did not present the legislation to the Assembly Health Committee as scheduled because it did not have enough votes to advance.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe panel includes multiple Democratic lawmakers from heavily Catholic districts in the Los Angeles area, where the archdiocese actively opposed the legislation.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-embed tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Ciframe width=\"540\" height=\"303\" allowfullscreen data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fnews.yahoo.com\u002Fvideo\u002Fmom-fights-die-her-own-231232919.html?format=embed\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fiframe\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003EYahoo Global News Anchor Katie Couric interviews O&#x2019;Donnell earlier this month. \u003C\u002Fb\u003E(Video: Yahoo News)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;We continue to work with Assembly members to ensure they are comfortable with the bill,&#x201D; Democratic Sens. Bill Monning of Carmel and Lois Wolk of Davis, and Assemblywoman Susan Eggman of Stockton said in a joint statement. &#x201C;We remain committed to passing the End of Life Option Act for all Californians who want and need the option of medical aid in dying.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EChristian Burkin, a spokesman for Eggman, said the bill could not meet the deadline to pass committees this year while lawmakers remained uncomfortable with the bill.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EReligious groups say allowing doctors to prescribe life-ending drugs is assisted suicide and goes against God&#x2019;s will. Religious opposition helped defeat similar legislation in California in 2007.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EMontana, Oregon, Vermont and Washington have court decisions or laws permitting doctors to prescribe life-ending drugs. A court ruling is pending in New Mexico.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAid-in-dying advocates hoped the tide would turn after national publicity surrounding 29-year-old Brittany Maynard, who moved from California to Oregon to legally end her life in November following a diagnosis of terminal brain cancer.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIn widely viewed videos and national media appearances, she said she deserved to get life-ending drugs in her home state of California. Maynard&#x2019;s family members advocated for the right-to-die bill in Sacramento after her death.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe bill had advanced out of the state Senate on a mostly party-line vote, with Democrats in support and Republicans opposed.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ECalifornia&#x2019;s bill was modeled on Oregon&#x2019;s law, which has been used in more than 750 deaths since voters approved it in 1994. Advocates for people with disabilities say terminally ill patients could be pressured to end their lives to avoid burdening their families.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe California Medical Association had dropped its decades-long opposition to aid-in-dying legislation, saying the decision should be left up to individual doctors if they want to help patients end their lives.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ELegislatures in Maine and Colorado have rejected right-to-die bills this year. Similar efforts have stalled in other Condition That&apos;s&#xA0;America&apos;s Costliest &#x2014; And One of Its Most Lethal\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003EOnly 44 percent of Americans had ever heard of this illness, but it&#x2019;s responsible for up to 50 percent of hospital deaths.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fb\u003E(AP Photo\u002FAl Behrman)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EMost Americans have never heard of sepsis, but the condition hospitalizes a million patients every year&#x2014;more than heart attack and stroke hospitalizations combined&#x2014;and is the nation&#x2019;s costliest reason for hospitalization, the \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Ftheconversation.com\u002Fsepsis-the-largely-unknown-condition-that-puts-one-million-people-in-the-hospital-each-year-43327\"\u003EConversation\u003C\u002Fa\u003E reports.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EYet it&#x2019;s hard to diagnose and many doctors don&#x2019;t look for, let alone spot, the deadly condition. So what is it?&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EOften confused with blood poisoning, sepsis occurs when the body responds in a toxic way to an infection (anything from pneumonia to a UTI). As the \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.sepsisalliance.org\u002Fnews\u002F2013\u002Ffour_in_ten_adults_never_heard_of_sepsis\u002F\"\u003ESepsis Alliance\u003C\u002Fa\u003E puts it, &#x201C;Your body&#x2019;s immune system, which is supposed to fight off the infection, goes into overdrive and begins to attack your body.&quot;&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ESepsis can cause tissue damage or multiple organ failure, landed 400,000 Medicare beneficiaries in ICUs across the country in 2013 alone, and plays a role in 33 percent to 50 percent of all US hospital deaths. It cost $5.5 billion for those initial Medicare hospitalizations in 2013, yet triggers return visits 40 percent of the time.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAnd as far as percentages go, here&#x2019;s another big one: A \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.hcup-us.ahrq.gov\u002Freports\u002Fstatbriefs\u002Fsb160.jsp\"\u003Ereport\u003C\u002Fa\u003E based on 2011 data found sepsis &quot;resulted in an aggregate cost of $20.3 billion or 5.2 percent&#x201D; of what America spent on all hospitalizations that year. Treatment may improve as hospitals create sepsis teams and new prediction tools, as well as investigate treatments; antibiotics and fluids alone can save lives, notes the Sepsis Alliance, which in 2013 reported only 44 percent of Americans had ever heard of sepsis.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EMeanwhile, experts are advising people with symptoms like depression, anxiety, forgetfulness, and weakness to seek faster hospitalization. Root causes include smoking, alcoholism, pollution, and pulmonary problems, a professor told \u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.frontline.in\u002Fstatic\u002Fhtml\u002Ffl2120\u002Fstories\u002F20041008001708600.htm\"\u003EFrontline\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E magazine years ago. But problems persist: In Canada, hundreds of malpractice cases in recent years involved sepsis, usually over poor diagnosis, the \u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fnews.nationalpost.com\u002Fnews\u002Fcanada\u002Finadequate-patient-assessment-canadian-doctors-missing-glaring-signs-of-sepsis\"\u003ENational Post\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E reports. Epidemic Numbers\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003EAs many as 8,200 people died from heroin overdoses in 2013 alone, according to a new CDC report. \u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E(Photo: Getty Images)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EHeroin overdose deaths in the United States nearly quadrupled between 2002 and 2013, fueled by lower costs as well as increased abuse of prescription opiate painkillers, \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.cdc.gov\u002Fvitalsigns\u002F\"\u003EU.S. health officials said on Tuesday\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe report found that heroin use increased by 63 percent from 2002 to 2013.&#xA0;In 2013, roughly 517,000 people reported that they had used heroin in the last year, a 150 percent increase from 2007. &#xA0;As many as 8,200 people died from heroin overdoses in 2013 alone.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ESuch medicines, which include Vicodin, OxyContin and Percocet, increase individuals&#x2019; susceptibility to heroin addiction, Dr. Thomas Frieden, director of the U.S. Centers for Disease Control and Prevention, told Reuters.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;Everything we see points to more accessible, less-expensive heroin all over the country,&#x201D; Frieden said of the joint report by the CDC and the U.S. Food and Drug Administration which analyzed national survey data on drug use from 2002 to 2013.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe report found that nearly all people (96 percent) who use heroin also use multiple other substances, and that the strongest risk factor for heroin abuse is prescription opiate abuse. &#xA0;In recent years people in nearly every demographic group are using the drug more: For example, heroin use has doubled among women.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAccording to the report, individuals who abuse prescription opiates have a 40 times greater risk of abusing heroin. The increased use has fueled sharp increases in overdose deaths.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EFrieden said reversing the trend will require an &#x201C;all-society response&#x201D; to improve opioid prescribing practices and expand access to effective treatment, increasing the use of drugs such as naloxone to reverse drug overdoses and working with law enforcement partners such as the Drug Enforcement Administration to disrupt the supply of heroin.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;There are lots of people who have not yet gotten an opiate and we need to protect them from the risk of getting addicted,&#x201D; Frieden said.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EHe said doctors are prescribing &#x201C;way too much of these medications, and the result of it is large numbers of people who are addicted.&#x201D;\u003Cb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERead This Next: \u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002Fare-you-a-sodium-sleuth-123472268522.html\"\u003EAre You a Sodium Sleuth?&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003ELet&#x2019;s keep in touch! Sleuth?\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003EA new government report suggests many Americans are trying to curb their sodium intake. If you&#x2019;re one, heed this advice.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E&#xA0;(Photo: Getty Images)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIf you are watchdogging the sodium in your diet, you are among friends. According to a recent study by the Centers for Disease Control and Prevention, more than 50 percent of adults living in 26 states, the District of Columbia and Puerto Rico are actively trying to reduce their sodium intake. This is good news, as the latest conclusion in the Scientific Report of the 2015 Dietary Guidelines Advisory Committee is that reducing the sodium in your diet can prevent and reduce high blood pressure.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAmerican adults are consuming more than 3,500 milligrams of sodium daily, which is way over the 2,300 mg upper limit recommended daily, and more than double the 1,500 mg that some folks, who are at a higher risk of getting high blood pressure, should be consuming. If you are age 51 and older, African-American or have diabetes, high blood pressure or kidney disease, you are in the higher risk group.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ESo, as a sodium sleuth, can you uncover which of the following is the No. 1 source of sodium in the diet of Americans? \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003Ea. Dairy foods (milk, yogurt and cheese)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003Eb. Condiments, gravies and salad dressings\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003Ec. Mixed dishes (pizza, burgers, soups, meat, chicken and fish dishes, grain dishes)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003Ed. Fruit juices\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EHere&#x2019;s your answer:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIt&#x2019;s those mixed dishes, which include burgers, pizza, seasoned grain dishes, main dinner entrees and soups that are the biggest sodium culprits in your diet. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIf these foods are routinely on your plate, snoop around the fast-food establishment&#x2019;s website prior to placing your order to find the lowest sodium option available. &#xA0;When food shopping, check the Nutrition Facts panel on the label to compare the amount of sodium per serving among the different brands of mixed dishes available. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EI did some sodium sleuthing myself, and this is what I found: That doesn&#x2019;t make sense to me,&#x201D; Staples told the newspaper.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EHis wife Kathleen Staples agrees, adding that there should be a training licensing program for the handling of fireworks, similar to the training for using motor vehicles.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E \n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"359\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F2825e2a3fff157b2bf8407636a02d24335d575dc.jpg\"\u003E \n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003ESales of fireworks are on the rise because state regulations are getting looser. \u003C\u002Fb\u003E(Photo: Getty Images)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EDevon Staples&#x2019; death wasn&#x2019;t the only serious fireworks-related incident over the holiday weekend. \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.indystar.com\u002Fstory\u002Fnews\u002F2015\u002F07\u002F06\u002Findiana-man-died-fireworks-accident\u002F29759329\u002F\"\u003ETwo men in Indiana\u003C\u002Fa\u003E were killed in two separate fireworks accidents, a \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.wmcactionnews5.com\u002Fstory\u002F29429502\u002F12-year-old-killed-in-fireworks-accident-in-nashville\"\u003E12-year-old boy in Nashville\u003C\u002Fa\u003E was killed after fireworks hit him in the chest, and a \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.usatoday.com\u002Fstory\u002Fnews\u002Fnation\u002F2015\u002F06\u002F29\u002Fmichigan-firework-death\u002F29470091\u002F\"\u003EDetroit man died\u003C\u002Fa\u003E after a fireworks shell he was holding to his head exploded. New York Giants defensive end Jason Pierre-Paul is still hospitalized after suffering a serious hand injury on Saturday while attempting to light fireworks. According to \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.nfl.com\u002Fnews\u002Fstory\u002F0ap3000000500185\u002Farticle\u002Fnew-york-giants-pull-60m-offer-to-jason-pierrepaul\"\u003ENFL.com\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, his $60 million long-term contract with the Giants may be withdrawn as a result.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EUnfortunately, injuries from fireworks aren&#x2019;t rare. According to the \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.aao.org\u002Fnewsroom\u002Fpolls-and-surveys\u002Ffireworks\"\u003E2015 Fireworks Safety Survey\u003C\u002Fa\u003E conducted by Harris Polls, nearly 30 percent of people know someone who has been injured by fireworks and almost 10 percent of people say they&#x2019;ve been injured by fireworks.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002Fbrain-science-explains-a-22-year-olds-fatal-123384333462.html\"\u003EBrain Science Explains This 22-Year-Old&#x2019;s Tragic Death by Fireworks\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EFireworks injuries are most common on the 4\u003Csup\u003Eth\u003C\u002Fsup\u003E of July and New Year&#x2019;s Eve, the \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.cdc.gov\u002Ffamily\u002Fminutes\u002Ftips\u002Ffireworks\u002F\"\u003ECenters for Disease Control and Prevention\u003C\u002Fa\u003E reports. But despite the headline-grabbing deaths this 4\u003Csup\u003Eth\u003C\u002Fsup\u003E of July, fireworks-related injuries are actually going down, fireworks expert Julie Heckman, executive director of the American Pyrotechnics Association, tells Yahoo Health &#x2014; even as people are buying the explosives at &#x201C;record levels.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EState regulations are getting looser&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ESales are on the rise, she says, because state regulations are getting looser: New York recently lifted its ban on fireworks and Georgia modified its law, echoing a trend in relaxing fireworks restrictions that started in 2000.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E \n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"319\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fdb248b5116ce746ec9e8b1544667bfb6345a7cc2.png\"\u003E \n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003EThe states labeled in blue allow some or all types of consumer fireworks permitted by federal regulations. States in white allow only wire or wood stick sparklers, and states in red ban all consumer fireworks. \u003C\u002Fb\u003E(Graphic: \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.americanpyro.com\u002F\"\u003EAmerican Pyrotechnics Association\u003C\u002Fa\u003E)&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ECurrently, consumer fireworks are only illegal in Delaware, Massachusetts, and New Jersey. Illinois, Iowa, Ohio, and Vermont allow only wire, wood-stick sparklers, and other novelty items, but the rest of the country allows some or all types of consumer fireworks that are permitted under federal regulations.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EHowever, Heckman says, fireworks regulations can vary from county to county. In certain parts of Maryland, for example, you can use ground-based sparklers, but they&#x2019;re banned in other counties.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EScott Wolfson, communications director for the U.S. Consumer Products Safety Commission, which regulates fireworks in the U.S. acknowledges that states regulations are becoming looser but warns that fireworks are still inherently dangerous.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;Our chairman, Elliott Kaye, respects that states can make their own decisions on the laws and rules for consumers and their state but he is concerned about the number and deaths and injuries that we are tracking each year for fireworks that tie to both legal and illegal products,&#x201D; Wolfson tells Yahoo Health.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EEach year, there are more than 10,000 fireworks-related injuries &#x2014; many of which are serious burns, says Wolfson. While the overall number of injuries that occur each year is on the decline, Wolfson says the number is still &#x201C;unacceptably high.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EIt sounds counterintuitive, but Heckman says the prevalence of fireworks makes it less likely that injuries will occur. &#x201C;When fireworks are permissible, people tend to take the time to plan their activity &#x2014; they think about where they&#x2019;re going to use the product and where spectators will be,&#x201D; she explains. &#x201C;When fireworks are not allowed and people choose to break the law, they&#x2019;re very careless. That&#x2019;s when we tend to see injuries and fires occur.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EOf course, banning fireworks doesn&#x2019;t mean people won&#x2019;t get their hands on them and Heckman points out that it&#x2019;s difficult to regulate fireworks use since police typically have more important things to do. People often carry them across state and county lines, but they&#x2019;ll also buy them on the black market&#x2026;and that&#x2019;s where it gets dangerous.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EFireworks are regulated by the U.S. Consumer Products Safety Commission, which has banned M-80 fireworks, quarter sticks, and cherry bombs. And all three can cause serious injury, says Heckman: &#x201C;A legal explosive will sting if you lit and held it in your hand; an illegal explosive will blow your hand off.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EHeckman stresses that it&#x2019;s crucial to read the instructions that come with fireworks and to steer clear of ones that seem to be duds for at least 20 minutes (and then douse them with water before approaching them).\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EHoping to light fireworks sometime this summer?&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ECall your local fire department to see what&#x2019;s allowed in your county and make sure the ones that you do buy are legal.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EAnd just because the 4\u003Csup\u003Eth\u003C\u002Fsup\u003E has passed, doesn&#x2019;t mean you&#x2019;re not at risk of an injury. Wolfson says about 70 percent of all injuries from fireworks occur in the 30 days leading up to and after the 4\u003Csup\u003Eth\u003C\u002Fsup\u003E. &#x201C;People still have leftover fireworks that they will be setting off,&#x201D; he explains.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EIf you&#x2019;re planning to set them off, only handle them when you&#x2019;re sober. Kathleen Staples admits her son had been drinking during his accident and says she hopes his death will remind people to that alcohol and fireworks don&#x2019;t mix. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;I spent 22 years keeping that boy safe,&#x201D; she told \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.cbsnews.com\u002Fnews\u002Fdevon-staples-man-killed-shooting-firework-off-head-thought-it-was-a-dud-mom-says\u002F\"\u003ECBS News\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. &#x201C;Do not drink, you need to have a designated sober person that is making life and death decisions with these things.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERead This Next: \u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002Fsnappers-sparklers-and-fireworks-meet-the-122185819157.html\"\u003EThe Unsuspecting Firework That Causes the Most Injuries&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003ELet&#x2019;s keep in touch! No wonder a new \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.sciencedaily.com\u002Freleases\u002F2015\u002F07\u002F150701123350.htm\"\u003Estudy\u003C\u002Fa\u003E from the University of Illinois at Urbana-Champaign found that on days when people eat at restaurants, they consume an extra 200 calories, as well as more fat and sodium. &#xA0;And the real shocker: It&#x2019;s not fast food that&#x2019;s the culprit. Women Spend Months Deciding\" width=\"512\" height=\"341\"\u003E \n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003ESimon Jersey thinks that wearing a uniform could give women back five months of their working lives.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E (Image via AP Photo\u002FKokomo Tribune, Kelly Lafferty Gerber)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EWoman sometimes get a bad rap for having a hard time deciding what to wear, but leave it to a uniform supplier to try to quantify just how much time they spend pondering outfits before heading out the door.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EA study of 2,000 women, commissioned by UK uniform supplier \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.simonjersey.com\u002FPagesPublic\u002FUserControlled\u002FUserDefined.aspx?page=What-To-Wear\"\u003ESimon Jersey\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, finds the average woman spends more than an hour per week &#x2014; for a total of three days each year or five months over a woman&#x2019;s working life from age 18 to 65 &#x2014; choosing what to wear. It breaks down to about 12 minutes every workday morning, 10 minutes every weekend morning, and about 27.5 minutes before a night out.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EYou think that&#x2019;s bad? Half of women also worry about their outfit the night before or before getting out of bed in the morning.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EEven with all that planning, two-thirds of women admit to trying on multiple outfits before leaving the house; about 15 percent have regretted their choice and returned to pick something else. It&#x2019;s no surprise, then, that about 25 percent say they&#x2019;ve arrived late to work because of deliberating what to wear.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EWhat&#x2019;s to consider exactly?&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EWell, 37 percent of women who say choosing an outfit is stressful cite concerns about whether their choice is suitable for work. Other worries relate to the dress code, weather, looks, and whether it&#x2019;s flattering.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ESimon Jersey concludes uniforms could save time and stress; its survey doesn&#x2019;t explore how long men stand in front of the closet, but \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.kirotv.com\u002Fnews\u002Fnews\u002Fnational\u002Fwomen-spend-5-months-their-working-lives-choosing-\u002FnmsP8\u002F?icmp=cmgcontent_internallink_relatedcontent_2014_partners1\"\u003EKIRO 7\u003C\u002Fa\u003E has a theory: &#x201C;They probably take just as long as women do. the Computer Game That Says It Can Help You Lose 1.5 Pounds in a Week","summary":"A computer game could help you put the brakes on unhealthy food  and lose weight.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fdiminuendo\u002F1.0\u002Foriginal\u002Fd37fde4ddab346027b5883ce2d0600794e1763a3.gif\" width=\"540\" height=\"305\" alt=\"Try the Computer Game That Says It Can Help You Lose 1.5 Pounds in a Week\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003EAn online game could train you to &#x201C;stop&#x201D; unhealthy foods and &#x201C;choose&#x201D; healthy options.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E (Photo: Corbis\u002FYahoo Health)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EHey Candy Crush addicts, those super-fast reflexes you&#x2019;ve been developing can finally be put to use &#x2014; with a game that research shows can actually help you lose weight.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EScientists from the University of Exeter and Cardiff University in the UK have created an \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Ffoodtraining.exeter.ac.uk\u002F\"\u003Eonline computer game\u003C\u002Fa\u003E that they say can help train people to resist unhealthy foods. Here&#x2019;s how it works: You have to repeatedly avoid pressing images of certain items (like cookies) while responding to other images (like fruit and clothes). The end result, researchers say, is that you&#x2019;re trained to associate unhealthy foods with &#x201C;stopping&#x201D; &#x2014; consequently avoiding them more in real life.&#xA0;\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIt may sound too good to be true, but their research has found it actually works on some people. The study, published in the journal \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.sciencedirect.com\u002Fscience\u002Farticle\u002Fpii\u002FS0195666314005194\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003EAppetite\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Ci\u003E,\u003C\u002Fi\u003E included more than 80 adults. Those who played the game lost an average of 1.5 pounds a week and ate 220 fewer calories a day. Study participants also reported that they didn&#x2019;t like the foods that they were trained to associate with &#x201C;stopping&#x201D; as much as they did before playing the game.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EInterested in trying the game out? You can play it \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Ffoodtraining.exeter.ac.uk\u002F\"\u003Ehere\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ECognitive neuroscientist and lead study researcher Natalia Lawrence, PhD, has been researching the concept for five years and tells Yahoo Health she&#x2019;s happy it so easily translated from the lab into real life. &#x201C;I was surprised that people lost weight in such a short period of time &#x2014; some colleagues suggested this wouldn&#x2019;t happen,&#x201D; she explains.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated:&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002Fthe-origin-of-a-craving-115402829598.html\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003EThe Origin Of A Craving\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWhile most people aren&#x2019;t exactly clamoring to go on a weight-loss plan, 88 percent of study participants said they would be happy to keep playing the game and would even recommend it to a friend.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBut how can pressing keys on a keyboard (or not, for that matter) have such an impact on what we eat? According to Lawrence, the regions of our brain that are associated with reward are also linked to movement. Therefore, training yourself to avoid pressing a key when you see certain foods can make you feel less of a reward with regard to that food.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWorth noting: The study only included people who said they were regular snackers and had some issues with controlling how much they ate, so more research is needed to determine whether it works for everyone.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated:&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002F9-foods-that-can-curb-your-sugar-cravings-103055811873.html\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003E9 Foods That Can Curb Your Sugar Cravings\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ELawrence also points out that the study was conducted over a short period of time, so researchers currently aren&#x2019;t sure what impact the game may have on a person&#x2019;s overall eating habits.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EOrlando-based psychologist&#xA0;Alan&#xA0;D.&#xA0;Keck, PsyD, says that given what we know about human behavior, the findings make sense. &#x201C;There are two common behavior-change processes going on at the same time in this game, and both have been found to be effective,&#x201D; he tells Yahoo Health.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe first &#x2014; having people choose healthy foods &#x2014; is typically the most effective for changing someone&#x2019;s behavior, he says, because it focuses more on what you want them to do rather than what you don&#x2019;t want them to do. When we&#x2019;re told not to do something (like don&#x2019;t eat a bag of cookies), we typically do it anyway, he says. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe second &#x2014; repeated exposure to bad foods and resisting them &#x2014; is a tactic that is often used with people with obsessive-compulsive disorder, Keck says: &#x201C;Every time you avoid the behavior, the impulse to have your usual response to it gets a little bit weaker.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ELawrence is hopeful that with more research and tweaking, the game could eventually be a new way to help people lose weight. &#x201C;I think this approach is one promising tool that could help to control cravings,&#x201D; she says.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERead This Next:&#xA0;\u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002F8-super-painless-ways-to-finally-nix-those-sugar-115886783798.html\"\u003E8 Super Painless Ways to Finally Nix Those Sugar Cravings\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003ELet&#x2019;s keep in touch! One\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003EStart in push-up position, your hands just inside the plane of your shoulders. Walk your feet up the wall, about a foot above the floor. Your body should form a rigid plank parallel to the ground. Squeeze your core throughout the move. With your feet still on the wall, do a single push-up, slowly lowering your chest to the floor and pressing back up.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"530\" height=\"430\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w530\u002Fe89652d7f14795e24e0de7ac39a0d7c4fb5e1d7b.gif\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EStep Two\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003ENext, keeping your spine and neck straight, walk your hands back toward the wall while stepping your feet up the wall until you&#x2019;re in a handstand position.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"368\" height=\"430\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w368\u002F8fc94f6aeaecc9bc57b4ec086882fef1172f5da7.gif\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EStep Three\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003EKeeping your toes on the wall, hold the handstand for a beat. Walk your hands back from the wall while stepping your feet back down the wall, returning to the start position. That&#x2019;s one. Did Women Start to Outlive Men?","summary":"Its well known that women live longer than men do, but this wasnt always the case.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F8de55a098c57ccc3b5f916997f582bd7cc239e31.jpg\" width=\"540\" height=\"404\" alt=\"When Did Women Start to Outlive Men?\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003ELadies can thank the late 1800s for their relative rise in longevity.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E (Photo: Getty Images)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIt&#x2019;s well known that women live longer than men do, but this wasn&#x2019;t always the case: A new study finds that differences between men and women&#x2019;s life expectancies began to emerge in the late 1800s.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EFor the study, researchers analyzed information from people born between 1800 and 1935 in 13 developed countries.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThey found that over this time period, death rates decreased among both men and women. But starting in 1880, death rates decreased much faster among women, leading to differences in mortality rates between the sexes.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe findings show that, although a greater \u003Ca\u003Elife expectancy for women\u003C\u002Fa\u003E is seen as normal today, it is actually &#x201C;a relatively new demographic phenomenon that emerged among people born in the late 19th century,&#x201D; the researchers concluded.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EFor example, among people born before 1840, death rates were about the same for men and women of a given age. But for people born between 1880 and 1899, death rates for men ages 50 to 70 were 1.5 times greater than those for women of the same age.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAmong people born after 1900, the death rate of 50- to 70-year-old men was double that of women of the same age, according to the study.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.livescience.com\u002F35863-grow-old-gracefully-tips.html\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003E8 Tips for Healthy Aging\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.livescience.com\u002F34733-heart-disease-high-cholesterol-heart-surgery.html\"\u003ECardiovascular disease\u003C\u002Fa\u003E was the main cause of the higher death rates among men, the researchers said. &#xA0;Heart disease and stroke accounted for more than 40 percent of the increase in male mortality rates versus female mortality rates between 1880 and 1919, the researchers noted.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBiologically, men may be more vulnerable to cardiovascular disease, but this susceptibility was seen only after deaths from other causes, such as infections, started to decline, the researchers said. &#xA0; \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBody fat (also called adiposity) tends to be distributed differently over men&#x2019;s bodies compared with women&#x2019;s, and &#x201C;their differing patterns of adiposity could make men more vulnerable to the increasing weight that resulted from changes in diet and activity,&#x201D; the researchers said in their study, published this week in the journal Proceedings of the National Academy of Sciences.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EFuture studies could investigate other differences between the sexes, including genetic dissimilarities, that may play a role in the increased risk of death from heart disease in men, the researchers said.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EMore from We break down the most common misconceptions about the mental condition.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F8e9b67140bba29ec86e4359cd83a3cc27f2d0096.jpg\" alt=\"What People Get Wrong About Bipolar Disorder\" width=\"540\" height=\"405\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003EThere&#x2019;s a lot you may not realize about this mental condition. \u003C\u002Fb\u003E(Photo:&#xA0;Corbis\u002FImage Source)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ETV programs like Showtime&#x2019;s \u003Ci\u003EShameless\u003C\u002Fi\u003E and \u003Ci\u003EHomeland \u003C\u002Fi\u003Eand movies like \u003Ci\u003EInfinitely Polar Bear \u003C\u002Fi\u003Ehave given bipolar disorder some significant screen time over the last few years. But how much about the entertainment industry&#x2019;s portrayal of the mental condition &#x2014; which affects approximately 5.7 million adults in the U.S. &#x2014; is actually \u003Ci\u003Eaccurate\u003C\u002Fi\u003E?\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;Bipolar disorder is a mental disorder characterized by periods of elevated mood, energy, and activity called manic episodes, and periods of depressive episodes,&#x201D; Amelia Davis, MD, the medical director at Rosewood Ranch in Wickenburg, Arizona, explains to Yahoo Health. &#x201C;The symptoms of bipolar disorder are severe and different from normal ups and downs that everyone goes through from time to time.&#x201D;&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ESome of Hollywood&#x2019;s portrayals of the disorder do stand true &#x2014; alcohol, caffeine, and recreational drugs can potentially trigger symptoms; sufferers often try to hide their illness at work; and there can be a strain on families trying to help loved ones who refuse treatment. But there are some aspects of the condition that are nothing more than myths.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EMyth: People with bipolar disorder experience several mood swings in the course of a few hours. \u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ESometimes, people experience mood swings that last a couple of hours and ask if they have bipolar disorder, Davis says. &#x201C;The mood and symptoms associated with bipolar disorder typically last several days and are more severe [than the average mood swing] and interfere with some aspects of the individual&#x2019;s ability to function,&#x201D; she says. Bipolar disorder also does not cause moods to switch back and forth rapidly, going from manic to depressive within a few hours. Instead, individuals with bipolar disorder typically have two to four mood cycles a year, according to Davis.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EMyth: When people are in the manic phase, they are often happy. \u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EManic episodes can actually make people angry, irritable, and aggressive, Davis says. &#x201C;People experiencing a manic episode often sleep very little, have increased energy, are talking very rapidly, and may appear hyperactive or involved in a lot of different activities, she explains.&#xA0;&#x201C;Some people can even become psychotic and have delusions or start hear voices that are not there.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated:&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002Fbipolar-disorder-what-you-need-to-know-108265401883.html\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003EBipolar Disorder: What You Need to Know\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EMyth: Bipolar disorder is easy to diagnose. \u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EProlonged periods of misdiagnosis are actually common, Natasha Tracy, the award-winning writer behind the blog \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fnatashatracy.com\u002Ftopic\u002Fbipolar-blog\u002F\"\u003EBipolar Burble\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, tells Yahoo Health. &#x201C;I sought treatment at the age of 20 and, at that time, I knew that I had bipolar disorder from the extensive research I had done,&#x201D; Tracy says. &#x201C;It took a change in doctors and about a year to be properly diagnosed &#x2014; though a diagnosis is really only the tip of the iceberg in terms of gaining any real sense of wellness.&#x201D;&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EMyth: You can take a quick test to diagnose bipolar disorder. \u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBipolar disorder tends to \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.nimh.nih.gov\u002Fhealth\u002Fpublications\u002Flooking-at-my-genes-what-can-they-tell-me\u002Findex.shtml\"\u003Erun in the family\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, according to the National Institute of Mental Health. If you have a close relative with the disorder, you may have a 10 percent chance of experiencing symptoms of a mood disorder such as bipolar disorder, but there is no sure-fire way to test for the mental illness. &#x201C;There is a test performed on saliva samples that looks for genetic mutations associated with the disorder, &#x201C; Reef Karim, DO, a human behavior expert, psychiatrist, and addiction medicine physician in Beverly Hills, California, tells Yahoo Health. &#x201C;But scientifically, we aren&#x2019;t at the place yet where we can determine from a test if someone is bipolar.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EMyth: It&#x2019;s impossible for people with bipolar disorder to lead normal, healthy lives. \u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EPeople with the condition can maintain healthy careers and relationships through treatment, such as medication and therapy. In addition to these options, &#x201C;individuals with bipolar disorder can help control their symptoms by getting enough sleep, having a regular sleeping schedule, exercising regularly, eating right, keeping stress low, and having supportive people in his or her life,&#x201D; Davis says.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated:&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002Fwhat-demi-lovato-wishes-people-understood-about-120104656347.html\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003EWhat Demi Lovato Wishes People Understood About Bipolar Disorder\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EMyth: Bipolar sufferers are \u003Ci\u003Ealways\u003C\u002Fi\u003E unstable. \u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EDuring a manic episode, individuals with bipolar disorder may engage in reckless behavior and poor judgment, Davis says. &#x201C;An individual may feel like they are on top of the world and act invincible, and in a depressive episode, individuals may feel extremely hopeless and have thoughts of ending his or her own life,&#x201D; she explains. But Tracy says that through her own illness, she also experiences periods of less symptomatic behavior she calls \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fbipolar.about.com\u002Fod\u002Fglossaryef\u002Fg\u002Fgl_euthymia.htm\"\u003Eeuthymia\u003C\u002Fa\u003E: a normal, non-depressed, positive (or neutral) mood.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EMyth: All people with bipolar disorder are geniuses. \u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe short-lived ABC show \u003Ci\u003EMind Games \u003C\u002Fi\u003Efeatured a character whose bipolar disorder made him brilliant in human psychology. But not everyone with bipolar disorder is highly intelligent. People with higher-than-average intelligence and lower-than-average intelligence are both likely to be hospitalized with bipolar disorder, according to a \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov\u002Fpubmed\u002F22472877\"\u003Estudy published in the \u003Ci\u003EJournal of Molecular Psychiatry\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. Tracy credits this myth to people&#x2019;s desire to find a higher meaning in mental illnesses. &#x201C;People who suffer, and those who see that suffering, want to believe that in the end, something good will come of it,&#x201D; Tracy writes in an \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.huffingtonpost.com\u002Fnatasha-tracy\u002Fdo-the-mentally-ill-have-_b_5393259.html\"\u003Eessay for The Huffington Post\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. &#x201C;But I can tell you, from the bottom of my heart: there is no upside to my bipolar disorder. I am sick. I hate being sick. I would give anything to give this particular &#x2018;gift&#x2019; away.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWhat are some of the biggest things people get wrong about being bipolar? We got some candid answers through Whisper, the free app that allows users to share their secrets anonymously.
